وَقَوْلُهُ: ﴿وَمَا كَانَ لَكُمْ أَنْ تُؤْذُوا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ وَلا أَنْ تَنْكِحُوا أَزْوَاجَهُ مِنْ بَعْدِهِ أَبَدًا إِنَّ ذَلِكُمْ كَانَ عِنْدَ اللَّهِ عَظِيمًا﴾ : قَالَ ابْنُ أَبِي حَاتِمٍ: حَدَّثَنَا عَلِيُّ بْنُ الْحُسَيْنِ، حَدَّثَنَا مُحَمَّدُ بْنُ أَبِي حَمَّادٍ، حَدَّثَنَا مهْرَان، عَنْ سُفْيَانَ، عَنْ دَاوُدَ بْنِ أَبِي هِنْدٍ، عَنْ عِكْرِمة، عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ فِي قَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى: ﴿وَمَا كَانَ لَكُمْ أَنْ تُؤْذُوا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ﴾ قَالَ: نَزَلَتْ فِي رَجُل هَمّ أَنْ يَتَزَوَّجَ بَعْضَ نِسَاءِ النَّبِيِّ ﷺ. قَالَ رَجُلٌ لِسُفْيَانَ: أَهِيَ عَائِشَةُ؟ قَالَ: قَدْ ذَكَرُوا ذَاكَ.

وَكَذَا قَالَ مُقَاتِلُ بْنِ حَيَّان، وَعَبْدِ الرَّحْمَنِ بْنِ زَيْدِ بْنِ أَسْلَمَ، وَذَكَرَ بِسَنَدِهِ عَنِ السُّدِّيِّ أَنَّ الَّذِي عَزَمَ عَلَى ذَلِكَ طَلْحَةُ بْنُ عُبَيْدِ اللَّهِ، رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ، حَتَّى نَزَلَ التَّنْبِيهُ عَلَى تَحْرِيمِ ذَلِكَ؛ وَلِهَذَا أَجْمَعَ الْعُلَمَاءُ قَاطِبَةً عَلَى أَنَّ مَنْ تُوُفِّيَ عَنْهَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ ﷺ مِنْ أَزْوَاجِهِ أَنَّهُ يَحْرُمُ عَلَى غَيْرِهِ تَزْوِيجُهَا مِنْ بَعْدِهِ؛ لِأَنَّهُنَّ أَزْوَاجُهُ فِي الدُّنْيَا وَالْآخِرَةِ وَأُمَّهَاتُ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ، كَمَا تَقَدَّمَ. وَاخْتَلَفُوا فِيمَنْ دَخَلَ بِهَا ثُمَّ طَلَّقَهَا فِي حَيَاتِهِ هَلْ يَحِلُّ لِغَيْرِهِ أَنْ يَتَزَوَّجَهَا؟ عَلَى قَوْلَيْنِ، مَأْخَذُهُمَا: هَلْ دَخَلَتْ هَذِهِ فِي عُمُومِ قَوْلِهِ: ﴿مِنْ بَعْدِهِ﴾ أَمْ لَا؟ فَأَمَّا مَنْ تَزَوَّجَهَا ثُمَّ طَلَّقَهَا قَبْلَ أَنْ يَدْخُلَ بِهَا، فَمَا نَعْلَمُ فِي حِلِّهَا لِغَيْرِهِ -وَالْحَالَةُ هَذِهِ -نِزَاعًا، وَاللَّهُ أَعْلَمُ.

وَقَالَ ابْنُ جَرِيرٍ: حَدَّثَنِي [مُحَمَّدُ] بْنُ الْمُثَنَّى، حَدَّثَنَا عَبْدُ الْوَهَّابِ، حَدَّثَنَا دَاوُدُ، عَنْ عَامِرٍ؛ أَنَّ نَبِيَّ اللَّهِ ﷺ مَاتَ وَقَدْ مَلَكَ قَيْلَةَ بِنْتَ الْأَشْعَثِ -يَعْنِي: ابْنَ قَيْسٍ -فَتَزَوَّجَهَا عِكْرِمَةُ بْنُ أَبِي جَهِلَ بَعْدَ ذَلِكَ، فَشَقَّ ذَلِكَ عَلَى أَبِي بَكْرٍ مَشَقَّةً شَدِيدَةً، فَقَالَ لَهُ عُمَرُ: يَا خَلِيفَةَ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ، إِنَّهَا لَيْسَتْ مِنْ نِسَائِهِ، إِنَّهَا لَمْ يُخَيّرها رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ، وَلَمْ يَحْجُبْهَا، وَقَدْ بَرَّأَهَا اللَّهُ مِنْهُ بِالرِّدَّةِ الَّتِي ارْتَدَتْ مَعَ قَوْمِهَا. قَالَ: فَاطْمَأَنَّ أَبُو بَكْرٍ، رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا وَسَكَنَ .

وَقَدْ عَظَّمَ اللَّهُ تَبَارَكَ وَتَعَالَى ذَلِكَ، وَشَدَّدَ فِيهِ وَتَوَعَّدَ عَلَيْهِ بِقَوْلِهِ: ﴿إِنَّ ذَلِكُمْ كَانَ عِنْدَ اللَّهِ عَظِيمًا﴾ ، ثُمَّ قَالَ: ﴿إِنْ تُبْدُوا شَيْئًا أَوْ تُخْفُوهُ فَإِنَّ اللَّهَ كَانَ بِكُلِّ شَيْءٍ عَلِيمًا﴾ أَيْ: مَهْمَا تُكِنُّهُ ضَمَائِرُكُمْ وَتَنْطَوِي عَلَيْهِ سَرَائِرُكُمْ، فَإِنَّ اللَّهَ يَعْلَمُهُ؛ فَإِنَّهُ لَا تَخْفَى عَلَيْهِ خَافِيَةٌ، ﴿يَعْلَمُ خَائِنَةَ الأعْيُنِ وَمَا تُخْفِي الصُّدُورُ﴾ [غَافِرٍ: ١٩] .

---

## 33:55 — verse 55

### Translation

When the Exalted commanded the women to observe veiling from unrelated men, He made clear that these relatives are not among those from whom veiling is obligatory, just as He excepted them in Surat al-Nur, at His saying: {And let them not display their adornment except to their husbands, or their fathers, or their husbands' fathers, or their sons, or their husbands' sons, or their brothers, or their brothers' sons, or their sisters' sons, or their women} to the end of the verse [al-Nur: 31], and it contains additions beyond these. Its exegesis and the discussion of it have already been given in a manner sufficient to make repeating it unnecessary. Some of the predecessors asked: why were the paternal uncle and the maternal uncle not mentioned in these two verses? Ikrimah and al-Sha'bi answered that they were not mentioned because they might describe her to their own sons.

Ibn Jarir said: Muhammad ibn al-Muthanna told me, Hajjaj ibn Minhal told us, Hammad told us, Dawud told us, from al-Sha'bi and Ikrimah, concerning His saying: {There is no blame upon them concerning their fathers, nor their sons, nor their brothers, nor their brothers' sons, nor their sisters' sons, nor their women, nor those whom their right hands possess}, I said: what is the matter with the paternal uncle and the maternal uncle, that they were not mentioned? They said: the two of them describe her to their own sons. And they disliked that a woman should remove her headcover in front of her maternal uncle or her paternal uncle.

His saying: {nor their women} means by that: there is no requirement of veiling from believing women.

His saying: {nor those whom their right hands possess} means by it: their slaves, both male and female, as was already noted, along with the citation of the hadith concerning it.

Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab said: it means by this only the slave women. Ibn Abi Hatim reported it.

His saying: {And fear Allah. Indeed Allah is Witness over all things} means: fear Him in private and in public, for He is Witness over all things, nothing hidden escapes Him, so let them be mindful of the One who watches.

### Source (Arabic) — review against this

لَمَّا أَمَرَ تَعَالَى النِّسَاءَ بِالْحِجَابِ مِنَ الْأَجَانِبِ، بيَّن أَنَّ هَؤُلَاءِ الْأَقَارِبَ لَا يَجِبُ الِاحْتِجَابُ مِنْهُمْ، كَمَا اسْتَثْنَاهُمْ فِي سُورَةِ النُّورِ، عِنْدَ قَوْلِهِ: ﴿وَلا يُبْدِينَ زِينَتَهُنَّ إِلا لِبُعُولَتِهِنَّ أَوْ آبَائِهِنَّ أَوْ آبَاءِ بُعُولَتِهِنَّ أَوْ أَبْنَائِهِنَّ أَوْ أَبْنَاءِ بُعُولَتِهِنَّ أَوْ إِخْوَانِهِنَّ أَوْ بَنِي إِخْوَانِهِنَّ أَوْ بَنِي أَخَوَاتِهِنَّ أَوْ نِسَائِهِنَّ﴾ إِلَى آخِرِهَا، [النُّورِ: ٣١] ، وَفِيهَا زِيَادَاتٌ عَلَى هَذِهِ. وَقَدْ تَقَدَّمَ تَفْسِيرُهَا وَالْكَلَامُ عَلَيْهَا بِمَا أَغْنَى عَنْ إِعَادَتِهِ. وَقَدْ سَأَلَ بَعْضُ السَّلَفِ فَقَالَ: لِم لَمْ يُذْكَرِ الْعَمُّ وَالْخَالُ فِي هَاتَيْنِ الْآيَتَيْنِ؟ فَأَجَابَ عِكْرِمَةُ وَالشَّعْبِيُّ: بِأَنَّهُمَا لَمْ يُذْكَرَا؛ لِأَنَّهُمَا قَدْ يَصِفَانِ ذَلِكَ لِبَنِيهِمَا. قَالَ ابْنُ جَرِيرٍ: حَدَّثَنِي مُحَمَّدُ بْنُ الْمُثَنَّى، حَدَّثَنَا حَجَّاجُ بْنُ مِنْهال، حَدَّثَنَا حَمَّادٌ، حَدَّثَنَا دَاوُدُ، عَنِ الشَّعْبِيِّ وَعِكْرِمَةَ فِي قَوْلِهِ: ﴿لَا جُنَاحَ عَلَيْهِنَّ فِي آبَائِهِنَّ وَلا أَبْنَائِهِنَّ وَلا إِخْوَانِهِنَّ وَلا أَبْنَاءِ إِخْوَانِهِنَّ وَلا أَبْنَاءِ أَخَوَاتِهِنَّ وَلا نِسَائِهِنَّ وَلا مَا مَلَكَتْ أَيْمَانُهُنَّ﴾ قُلْتُ: مَا شَأْنُ الْعَمِّ وَالْخَالِ لَمْ يُذْكَرَا؟ قَالَا هُمَا يَنْعَتَانِهَا لِأَبْنَائِهِمَا. وَكَرِهَا أَنْ تَضَعَ خِمَارَهَا عِنْدَ خَالِهَا وَعَمِّهَا.

* *

وَقَوْلُهُ: ﴿وَلا نِسَائِهِنَّ﴾ : يَعْنِي بِذَلِكَ: عَدَم الِاحْتِجَابِ مِنَ النِّسَاءِ الْمُؤْمِنَاتِ.

* *

وَقَوْلُهُ: ﴿وَلا مَا مَلَكَتْ أَيْمَانُهُنَّ﴾ يَعْنِي بِهِ: أرقاءَهن مِنَ الذُّكُورِ وَالْإِنَاثِ، كَمَا تَقَدَّمَ التَّنْبِيهُ عَلَيْهِ، وَإِيرَادُ الْحَدِيثِ فِيهِ .

قَالَ سَعِيدُ بْنُ الْمُسَيَّبِ: إِنَّمَا يَعْنِي بِهِ: الْإِمَاءَ فَقَطْ. رَوَاهُ ابْنُ أَبِي حَاتِمٍ.

* *

وَقَوْلُهُ: ﴿وَاتَّقِينَ اللَّهَ إِنَّ اللَّهَ كَانَ عَلَى كُلِّ شَيْءٍ شَهِيدًا﴾ أَيْ: وَاخْشَيْنَهُ فِي الْخَلْوَةِ وَالْعَلَانِيَةِ، فَإِنَّهُ شَهِيدٌ عَلَى كُلِّ شَيْءٍ، لَا تخفى عليه خافية، فراقبن الرقيب.

---

## 33:56 — verse 56

### Translation

Al-Bukhari said: Abu al-Aliyah said: The salah (prayer/blessing) of Allah is His praise of him before the angels, and the salah of the angels is supplication. Ibn Abbas said: "they perform salah upon him" means they bless him. Al-Bukhari related both of these as suspended reports (ta'liq) from them.

Abu Ja'far al-Razi related it from al-Rabi' ibn Anas, from Abu al-Aliyah, likewise. The same was related from al-Rabi' as well. Ali ibn Abi Talhah related from Ibn Abbas exactly as he had said. Both of these were related by Ibn Abi Hatim.

Abu Isa al-Tirmidhi said: It was related from Sufyan al-Thawri and more than one of the scholars that they said: The salah of the Lord is mercy, and the salah of the angels is asking forgiveness.

Then Ibn Abi Hatim said: [chain] Al-A'mash, from Amr ibn Murrah, and al-A'mash also said, from Ata' ibn Abi Rabah, regarding {Indeed Allah and His angels perform salah upon the Prophet}: he said: His salah, Blessed and Exalted is He, is: "Subbuh, Quddus (Glorified, Most Holy), My mercy precedes My wrath."

The point of this verse is that Allah, Glorified is He, informed His servants of the rank of His servant and Prophet in His sight, in the highest assembly, that He praises him before the angels brought near, and that the angels perform salah upon him. Then He, Exalted is He, commanded the inhabitants of the lower world to perform salah and give the greeting of peace upon him, so that the praise of him would be gathered together from the inhabitants of both the higher and lower worlds.

Ibn Abi Hatim said: [chain] Ali ibn al-Husayn, from Ahmad ibn Abd al-Rahman, from his father, from his father, from Ash'ath ibn Ishaq, from Ja'far, meaning Ibn al-Mughirah, from Sa'id ibn Jubayr, from Ibn Abbas: that the Children of Israel said to Musa (peace be upon him): "Does your Lord perform salah?" So his Lord called out to him: "O Musa, they asked you, 'Does your Lord perform salah?' So say: Yes, I and My angels only perform salah upon My prophets and My messengers." Then Allah, Mighty and Majestic is He, revealed to His Prophet ﷺ: {Indeed Allah and His angels perform salah upon the Prophet. O you who believe, invoke salah upon him and greet him with a worthy greeting of peace.}

He, Glorified and Exalted is He, has informed that He performs salah upon His believing servants in His saying, Exalted is He: {O you who believe, remember Allah with much remembrance, and glorify Him morning and evening. It is He who performs salah upon you, and His angels, that He may bring you out from darkness into light, and He is ever Merciful to the believers} [al-Ahzab: 41-43]. And He, Exalted is He, said: {And give good tidings to the patient, those who, when a calamity befalls them, say: "Indeed we belong to Allah and indeed to Him we shall return." Upon those are blessings (salawat) from their Lord, and mercy, and it is those who are the rightly guided} [al-Baqarah: 155-157]. And in the hadith: "Indeed Allah and His angels perform salah upon those on the right sides of the rows." And in another hadith: "O Allah, bless the family of Abu Awfa." And the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said to the wife of Jabir, when she had asked him to invoke blessing upon her and her husband: "May Allah bless you and your husband."

Mutawatir (mass-transmitted) hadiths have come from the Messenger of Allah ﷺ commanding that salah be invoked upon him, and describing how it should be done, and we will mention, if Allah wills, whatever is feasible of them. Allah is the one whose help is sought.

Al-Bukhari said, in the commentary on this verse: [chain] Mis'ar, from al-Hakam, from Ibn Abi Layla, from Ka'b ibn Ujrah, who said: It was said, "O Messenger of Allah, as for the greeting of peace upon you, we already know it, but how is the salah?" He said: "Say: O Allah, send salah upon Muhammad and upon the family of Muhammad, [as You sent salah upon the family of Ibrahim, indeed You are Praiseworthy, Glorious. O Allah, bless Muhammad and the family of Muhammad] as You blessed the family of Ibrahim, indeed You are Praiseworthy, Glorious."

Imam Ahmad said: [chain] Shu'bah, from al-Hakam, who said: I heard Ibn Abi Layla say: Ka'b ibn Ujrah met me and said: "Shall I not give you a gift? The Messenger of Allah ﷺ came out to us and we said, 'O Messenger of Allah, we already know, or we already recognize, how to greet you with peace, but how is the salah?' He said: 'Say: O Allah, send salah upon Muhammad and upon the family of Muhammad, as You sent salah upon the family of Ibrahim, indeed You are Praiseworthy, Glorious. O Allah, bless Muhammad and the family of Muhammad, as You blessed the family of Ibrahim, indeed You are Praiseworthy, Glorious.'"

This hadith was related by the group (the compilers of the major hadith collections) in their books, through multiple chains, from al-Hakam, that is Ibn Utbah. Al-Bukhari added: and Abd Allah ibn Isa, both of them from Abd al-Rahman ibn Abi Layla, and he mentioned it.

Ibn Abi Hatim said: [chain] Hushaym ibn Bushayr, from Yazid ibn Abi Ziyad, from Abd al-Rahman ibn Abi Layla, from Ka'b ibn Ujrah, who said: When {Indeed Allah and His angels perform salah upon the Prophet. O you who believe, invoke salah upon him and greet him with a worthy greeting of peace} was revealed, he said: We said, "O Messenger of Allah, we already know the greeting of peace, but how is the salah upon you?" He said: "Say: O Allah, send salah upon Muhammad and upon the family of Muhammad, as You sent salah upon Ibrahim and upon the family of Ibrahim, indeed You are Praiseworthy, Glorious. And bless Muhammad and the family of Muhammad, as You blessed Ibrahim and the family of Ibrahim, indeed You are Praiseworthy, Glorious." And Abd al-Rahman ibn Abi Layla used to say: "and upon us along with them."

Al-Tirmidhi related it with this addition.

The meaning of their saying, "as for the greeting of peace upon you, we already know it," is that which is in the tashahhud (testimony recited in prayer) which he used to teach them, just as he used to teach them a surah of the Qur'an, and in it: "Peace be upon you, O Prophet, and the mercy of Allah and His blessings."

Another hadith: Al-Bukhari said: [chain] al-Layth, from Ibn al-Had, from Abd Allah ibn Khabbab, from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri, may Allah be pleased with him, who said: We said, "O Messenger of Allah, this is the greeting of peace, so how do we invoke salah upon you?" He said: "Say: O Allah, send salah upon Muhammad, Your servant and Your messenger, as You sent salah upon the family of Ibrahim. And bless Muhammad and the family of Muhammad, as You blessed the family of Ibrahim." [In another narration]: Abu Salih said, from al-Layth: "upon Muhammad and upon the family of Muhammad, as You blessed the family of Ibrahim."

[chain] Ibn Abi Hazim and al-Darawardi, from Yazid, meaning Ibn al-Had, who said: "as You sent salah upon Ibrahim, and bless Muhammad and the family of Muhammad, as You blessed Ibrahim and the family of Ibrahim."

Al-Nasa'i and Ibn Majah related it, from the hadith of Ibn al-Had, with the same chain.

Another hadith: Imam Ahmad said: I read to Abd al-Rahman: Malik, from Abd Allah ibn Abi Bakr, from his father, from Amr ibn Sulaym, who said: Abu Humayd al-Sa'idi informed me that they said, "O Messenger of Allah, how do we invoke salah upon you?" He said: "Say: O Allah, send salah upon Muhammad and his wives and his descendants, as You sent salah upon the family of Ibrahim, and bless Muhammad and his wives and his descendants, as You blessed the family of Ibrahim, indeed You are Praiseworthy, Glorious."

The rest of the group, besides al-Tirmidhi, related it from the hadith of Malik, with the same chain.

Another hadith: Muslim said: [chain] I read to Malik, from Nu'aym ibn Abd Allah al-Mujmir: Muhammad ibn Abd Allah ibn Zayd al-Ansari, he said: and Abd Allah ibn Zayd is the one who was shown the call to prayer in a vision, informed him, from Abu Mas'ud al-Ansari, who said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ came to us while we were in the gathering of Sa'd ibn Ubadah, and Bashir ibn Sa'd said to him, "Allah has commanded us to invoke salah upon you, O Messenger of Allah, so how do we invoke salah upon you?" He said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ then fell silent, until we wished that he had not asked him, then the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: "Say: O Allah, send salah upon Muhammad and upon the family of Muhammad, as You sent salah upon the family of Ibrahim, and bless Muhammad and the family of Muhammad, as You blessed the family of Ibrahim among all the worlds, indeed You are Praiseworthy, Glorious. And the greeting of peace is as you already know."

Abu Dawud, al-Tirmidhi, and al-Nasa'i related it from the hadith of Malik, with the same chain. Al-Tirmidhi said: hasan sahih (good and authentic).

Imam Ahmad, Abu Dawud, al-Nasa'i, Ibn Khuzaymah, Ibn Hibban, and al-Hakim in his Mustadrak related, from the hadith of Muhammad ibn Ishaq, from Muhammad ibn Ibrahim al-Taymi, from Muhammad ibn Abd Allah ibn Zayd ibn Abd Rabbih, from Abu Mas'ud al-Badri, that they said: O Messenger of Allah, as for the salam we already know it, so how should we send salat upon you when we perform salat in our prayer? He said: "Say: O Allah, send salat upon Muhammad and upon the family of Muhammad..." and he mentioned the rest.

Al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, related it in his Musnad from Abu Hurayrah, in like manner. It is from this that al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, held that it is obligatory upon the one praying to send salat upon the Messenger of Allah ﷺ in the final tashahhud (testimony), and that if he omits it, his prayer is not valid. Some later Maliki scholars and others began to censure Imam al-Shafi'i for making this a condition of the prayer, claiming that he was alone in holding this view. Abu Ja'far al-Tabari, al-Tahawi, al-Khattabi, and others reported a consensus (ijma') against this position, as transmitted by Qadi Iyad. But the one making this claim strained himself in his rebuttal of al-Shafi'i and forced the assertion of consensus on this matter, [and said what he did not have full knowledge of]. For we have related the obligation of this, and the command to send salat upon the Messenger of Allah ﷺ within the prayer, as is apparent from the verse itself, and as explained by this hadith, from a group of the companions, among them Ibn Mas'ud, Abu Mas'ud al-Badri, and Jabir ibn Abd Allah, and from the successors (tabi'in): al-Sha'bi, Abu Ja'far al-Baqir, and Muqatil ibn Hayyan. This is the view held by al-Shafi'i, with no disagreement reported from him on this, nor among his companions either. Imam Ahmad also came to hold this view in his later position, as reported from him by Abu Zur'ah al-Dimashqi. Ishaq ibn Rahawayh held the same, as did the jurist Imam Muhammad ibn Ibrahim, known as Ibn al-Mawwaz al-Maliki, may Allah have mercy on them all. Indeed, some of the leading Hanbali scholars held it obligatory to say the salat upon him ﷺ exactly as he taught them to say it when they asked him. And some of our companions (the Shafi'is) even held that sending salat upon the family (al) is likewise obligatory, a position reported by al-Bandaniji, Sulaym al-Razi, and his companion Nasr ibn Ibrahim al-Maqdisi, and transmitted by Imam al-Haramayn and his companion al-Ghazali as a stated view of al-Shafi'i. The correct position is that this is merely one accepted view (wajh), while the majority hold otherwise, and they report a consensus against it. Yet the apparent sense of the hadith supports the view of its obligation. And Allah knows best.

The point is that al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, in holding the obligation of sending salat upon the Prophet ﷺ within the prayer, has predecessors and successors as has been shown, praise and grace be to Allah. So there is no consensus against him on this matter, neither of old nor in more recent times. And Allah knows best.

Supporting this is another hadith related by Imam Ahmad, Abu Dawud, al-Tirmidhi (who deemed it sound), al-Nasa'i, Ibn Khuzaymah, and Ibn Hibban in their two Sahihs, from the narration of Haywah ibn Shurayh al-Misri, from Abu Hani' Humayd ibn Hani', from Amr ibn Malik Abu Ali al-Janbi, from Fadalah ibn Ubayd, may Allah be pleased with him, who said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ heard a man supplicating in his prayer who had not glorified Allah nor sent salat upon the Prophet ﷺ. The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: "This one has hastened." Then he called him and said to him and to others: "When any of you prays, let him begin by praising Allah, Mighty and Majestic, and extolling Him, then let him send salat upon the Prophet, then let him supplicate afterward for whatever he wishes."

Likewise the hadith related by Ibn Majah, from the narration of Abd al-Muhaymin ibn Abbas ibn Sahl ibn Sa'd al-Sa'idi, from his father, from his grandfather, from the Messenger of Allah ﷺ, that he said: "There is no prayer for one who has no ablution, and no ablution for one who does not mention the name of Allah over it, and no prayer for one who does not send salat upon the Prophet, and no prayer (that is complete) for one who does not love the Ansar."

However, this Abd al-Muhaymin is a discarded narrator (matruk). Al-Tabarani related it also from the narration of his brother, Ubayy ibn Abbas, but there is doubt regarding that too. It is known chiefly through the narration of Abd al-Muhaymin. And Allah knows best.

Another hadith: Imam Ahmad said: Yazid ibn Harun told us, Isma'il informed us, from Abu Dawud al-A'ma, from Burayda, who said: We said: O Messenger of Allah, we already know how to send salam upon you, so how do we send salat upon you? He said: "Say: O Allah, place Your salat, mercy, and blessings upon Muhammad and upon the family of Muhammad, as You placed them upon Abraham and the family of Abraham. Indeed You are Praiseworthy, Glorious."

Abu Dawud al-A'ma's name is Nufay' ibn al-Harith, and he is a discarded narrator (matruk).

Another report, halted (mawquf): We related it through the path of Sa'id ibn Mansur, Zayd ibn al-Hubab, and Yazid ibn Harun, all three from Nuh ibn Qays: Salamah al-Kindi told us, that Ali, may Allah be pleased with him, used to teach the people this supplication: "O Allah, Spreader of the outspread lands, Originator of the raised heavens, Shaper of hearts upon their natural disposition, whether wretched or blessed. Place the noblest of Your prayers, the growing increase of Your blessings, and the tenderness of Your compassion upon Muhammad, Your servant and messenger, the seal of what came before, the opener of what was closed, the proclaimer of truth by truth, the crusher of the armies of falsehood, just as he was entrusted and rose to bear Your command in obedience to You, hastening toward what pleases You, unwavering in step, unfaltering in resolve, retaining Your revelation, safeguarding Your covenant, pressing forward in carrying out Your command, until he kindled a firebrand for whoever would take fire from it. The bounties of Allah reach His people through his means. Through him hearts were guided after plunging into trials and sin, [and he established] clarifying signs, illuminating lights of Islam, and radiant judgments. He is Your trusted, faithful one, the keeper of Your stored knowledge, Your witness on the Day of Judgment, sent forth as a mercy, and Your messenger with the truth as compassion. O Allah, grant him ample room in Your justice, and reward him with the doubled measure of good from Your bounty, joys free of any taint, from the triumph of Your assured reward and the abundance of Your beautiful gift. O Allah, raise his structure above the structures of all builders, and honor his dwelling place and abode with You. Complete his light for him, and reward him, for having sent him forth, with acceptance of his testimony, approval of his speech, just utterance, decisive judgment, and mighty proof and argument."

This is a well known saying of Ali, may Allah be pleased with him. Ibn Qutaybah discussed it in Mushkil al-Hadith, as did Abu al-Husayn Ahmad ibn Faris the lexicographer in a treatise he compiled on the merit of sending salat upon the Prophet ﷺ, though there is doubt regarding its chain of transmission.

Our teacher, the hadith master Abu al-Hajjaj al-Mizzi, said: this Salamah al-Kindi is not well known, and did not meet Ali. That is what he said. But the hadith master Abu al-Qasim al-Tabarani related this report from Muhammad ibn Ali al-Sa'igh, from Sa'id ibn Mansur, who said: Nuh ibn Qays told us, from Salamah al-Kindi, who said: Ali, may Allah be pleased with him, used to teach us the salat upon the Prophet ﷺ, saying: "O Allah, Spreader of the outspread lands..." and he mentioned the rest.

Another report, halted (mawquf): Ibn Majah said: [Al-Husayn ibn Bayan told us], Ziyad ibn Abd Allah told us, al-Mas'udi told us, from Awn ibn Abd Allah, from Abu Fakhitah, from al-Aswad ibn Yazid, from Abd Allah ibn Mas'ud, may Allah be pleased with him, who said: When you send salat upon the Messenger of Allah ﷺ, do it well, for you do not know, perhaps it will be presented to him. They said to him: Then teach us. He said: Say: "O Allah, place Your salat, mercy, and blessings upon the master of the messengers, the leader of the God fearing, the seal of the prophets, Muhammad, Your servant and messenger, leader of good and guide to good, and messenger of mercy. O Allah, raise him to a praised station that the first and the last will envy him for. O Allah, send salat upon Muhammad [and upon the family of Muhammad] as You sent salat upon Abraham and upon the family of Abraham. Indeed You are Praiseworthy, Glorious. O Allah, bless Muhammad and the family of Muhammad as You blessed Abraham and the family of Abraham. Indeed You are Praiseworthy, Glorious."

This is a halted report (mawquf). Isma'il al-Qadi related something close to this from Abd Allah ibn Amr, or Umar, the narrator being uncertain which.

Another hadith: Ibn Jarir said: Abu Kurayb told us, Malik ibn Isma'il told us, Abu Isra'il told us, from Yunus ibn Khabbab, who said: He delivered a sermon to us in Persia and said: {Indeed Allah and His angels send salat upon the Prophet. O you who believe, send salat upon him and greet him with peace.} Then he said: someone informed me who heard Ibn Abbas say: thus was it revealed.

We said, or they said: "O Messenger of Allah, you have taught us the salam upon you, but how should we send salah upon you?" He said: "O Allah, send salah upon Muhammad and upon the family of Muhammad, as You sent salah upon Ibrahim and the family of Ibrahim, indeed You are Hamid (Praiseworthy), Majid (Glorious). And have mercy upon Muhammad and the family of Muhammad, as You had mercy upon the family of Ibrahim, indeed You are Hamid, Majid. [And bless Muhammad and the family of Muhammad, as You blessed Ibrahim, indeed You are Hamid, Majid.]"

Those who hold the view that supplicating mercy (tarahhum) upon the Prophet ﷺ is permissible use this hadith as evidence, this being the position of the majority. It is supported by the hadith of the bedouin who said: "O Allah, have mercy on me and on Muhammad, and have mercy on no one else besides us." The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: "You have narrowed something vast."

Al-Qadi Iyad related from the majority of the Malikis that they forbade this, and said that Abu Muhammad ibn Abi Zayd permitted it.

Another hadith: Imam Ahmad said: [chain] Muhammad ibn Ja'far, informed us Shu'bah, from Asim ibn Ubayd Allah who said: I heard Abd Allah ibn Amir ibn Rabi'ah narrating from his father who said: I heard the Prophet ﷺ say: "Whoever sends one salah upon me, the angels continue to send salah upon him for as long as he sends salah upon me, so let a servant do it little or much."

Ibn Majah related it from the hadith of Shu'bah, with the same chain.

Another hadith: Imam Ahmad said: [chain] Abu Salamah Mansur ibn Salamah al-Khuza'i and Yunus ibn Muhammad, both said: told us Layth, from Yazid ibn al-Had, from Amr ibn Abi Amr, from Abu al-Huwayrith, from Muhammad ibn Jubayr ibn Mut'im, from Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf who said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ went out and I followed him until he entered a palm grove and prostrated, prolonging the prostration until I feared, or was afraid, that Allah had taken his soul or seized him. He said: I came to look, and he raised his head and said: "What is the matter with you, O Abd al-Rahman?" He said: So I mentioned that to him, and he said: "Indeed Jibril (peace be upon him) said to me: Shall I not give you glad tidings? Indeed Allah, Mighty and Majestic, says: Whoever sends salah upon you, I send salah upon him, and whoever sends salam upon you, I send salam upon him."

Another route: Imam Ahmad said: [chain] Abu Sa'id, freedman of the Banu Hashim, told us Sulayman ibn Bilal, told us Amr ibn Abi Amr, from Abd al-Wahid ibn Muhammad ibn Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf, from Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf who said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ went out heading toward his charitable land, and he entered it and faced the qiblah, then fell down prostrating and prolonged the prostration, until I thought that Allah had taken his soul during it. I drew near to him and then sat down. He raised his head and said: "Who is this?" I said: Abd al-Rahman. He said: "What is your matter?" I said: O Messenger of Allah, you performed a prostration such that I feared Allah, Mighty and Majestic, had taken your soul during it. He said: "Indeed Jibril came to me and gave me the glad tiding that Allah, Mighty and Majestic, says to you: Whoever sends salah upon you, I send salah upon him, and whoever sends salam upon you, I send salam upon him, so I prostrated to Allah, Mighty and Majestic, in gratitude."

Another hadith: Al-Hafiz Abu al-Qasim al-Tabarani said: [chain] Muhammad ibn Abd al-Rahim ibn Bahir ibn Abd Allah ibn Mu'awiyah ibn Bahir ibn Raysan, told us Amr ibn al-Rabi' ibn Tariqah, told us Yahya ibn Ayyub, told us Abd Allah ibn Umar, from al-Hakam ibn Utaybah, from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i, from al-Aswad ibn Yazid, from Umar ibn al-Khattab, may Allah be pleased with him, who said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ went out for a need and found no one to accompany him. Umar became alarmed, and brought a vessel of water for purification, following behind him. He found the Prophet ﷺ prostrating in an upper chamber, and he withdrew from behind him until the Prophet ﷺ raised his head. He said: "You did well, O Umar, when you found me prostrating and withdrew from me. Indeed Jibril came to me and said: Whoever from your nation sends one salah upon you, Allah sends ten salahs upon him and raises him ten degrees."

Al-Hafiz al-Diya al-Maqdisi selected this hadith in his book al-Mustakhraj ala al-Sahihayn.

Isma'il al-Qadi related it from al-Qa'nabi, from Salamah ibn Wardan, from Anas, from Umar, in similar wording.

He also related it from Ya'qub ibn Humayd, from Anas ibn Iyad, from Salamah ibn Wardan, from Malik ibn Aws ibn al-Hadathan, from Umar ibn al-Khattab, in similar wording.

Another hadith: Abu Isa al-Tirmidhi said: [chain] Bundar, told us Muhammad ibn Khalid ibn Athmah, told me Musa ibn Ya'qub al-Zam'i, told me Abd Allah ibn Kaysan, that Abd Allah ibn Shaddad informed him, from Abd Allah ibn Mas'ud, that the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: "The people most entitled to me on the Day of Resurrection are those who send the most salah upon me."

Al-Tirmidhi, may Allah have mercy on him, alone related this, then said: This is a hasan gharib (sound, singular) hadith.

Another hadith: Isma'il al-Qadi said: [chain] Ali ibn Abd Allah, told us Sufyan, from Ya'qub ibn Zayd ibn Talhah who said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: "One who comes from my Lord came to me and said to me: There is no servant who sends one salah upon you but Allah sends ten upon him because of it." A man stood up and said: O Messenger of Allah, shall I not make half of my supplication for you? He said: "If you wish." He said: Shall I not make two thirds of my supplication for you? He said: "If you wish." He said: Shall I not make all of my supplication for you? He said: "Then Allah will suffice you the concern of this world and the concern of the next." A shaykh who was in Makkah, called Mani', said to Sufyan: From whom did you trace it? He said: I do not know.

Another hadith: Isma'il al-Qadi said: [chain] Sa'id ibn Salam al-Attar, told us Sufyan, meaning al-Thawri, from Abd Allah ibn Muhammad ibn Aqil, from al-Tufayl ibn Ubayy ibn Ka'b, from his father who said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ used to go out in the depth of the night and say: "The Rajifah (the first quaking) has come, followed by the Radifah (the second quaking that follows it), death has come with what is in it." Ubayy said: O Messenger of Allah, I pray during the night, shall I devote a third of my prayer to you? The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: "Half." He said: Shall I devote half of my prayer to you? The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: "Two thirds." He said: Shall I devote all of my prayer to you? He said: "Then Allah will forgive all your sins."

Al-Tirmidhi related it in similar wording, saying: [chain] Hannad, told us Qabisah, told us Sufyan, from Abd Allah ibn Muhammad ibn Aqil, from al-Tufayl ibn Ubayy ibn Ka'b, from his father who said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ, when two thirds of the night had passed, would rise and say: "O people, remember Allah, remember Allah, the Rajifah has come, followed by the Radifah, death has come with what is in it, death has come with what is in it." Ubayy said: I said: O Messenger of Allah, I send much salah upon you, how much of my prayer should I devote to you? He said: "As you wish." I said: A quarter? He said: "As you wish, but if you increase it, it is better for you." I said: Then half? He said: "As you wish, but if you increase it, it is better for you." I said: Then two thirds? He said: "As you wish, but if you increase it, it is better for you." I said: Shall I devote all of my prayer to you? He said: "Then your concern will be sufficed for you, and your sin will be forgiven."

Then he said: This is a hasan hadith.

Imam Ahmad said: [chain] Waki', told us Sufyan, from Abd Allah ibn Muhammad ibn Aqil, from al-Tufayl ibn Ubayy, from his father who said: A man said: O Messenger of Allah, what do you think if I devote all of my prayer to you? He said: "Then Allah will suffice you for what concerns you of your worldly life and your afterlife."

Another hadith: Imam Ahmad said: [chain] Abu Kamil, told us Hammad ibn Salamah, from Thabit, from Sulayman the freedman of al-Hasan ibn Ali, from Abd Allah ibn Abi Talhah, from his father, that the Messenger of Allah, Allah's peace and blessings be upon him, came one day with joy visible on his face. They said: O Messenger of Allah, we see joy on your face. He said: "Indeed the angel came to me and said: O Muhammad, does it not please you that your Lord, Mighty and Majestic, says: No one from your nation sends salah upon you but I send ten upon him, and no one from your nation sends salam upon you but I send ten upon him? He said: Yes indeed."

Al-Nasa'i related it from the hadith of Hammad ibn Salamah, with the same chain. Isma'il al-Qadi related it from Isma'il ibn Abi Uways, from his brother, from Sulayman ibn Bilal, from Ubayd Allah ibn Umar, from Thabit, from Abu Talhah, in similar wording.

Another route: [Imam] Ahmad said: Surayj narrated to us, Abu Ma'shar narrated to us, from Ishaq ibn Ka'b ibn Ujrah, from Abu Talhah al-Ansari, who said: One day the Messenger of Allah ﷺ awoke in good spirits, and cheerfulness could be seen on his face. They said: O Messenger of Allah, you have awoken today in good spirits, and cheerfulness can be seen on your face? He said: "Indeed, one who came to me from my Lord, Mighty and Majestic, came and said: Whoever among your community sends a single prayer of blessing upon you, Allah will record for him ten good deeds for it, erase from him ten bad deeds, raise him ten degrees, and return to him the like of it."

This too is a sound chain, and they did not include it among their collections.

Another hadith: Muslim, Abu Dawud, al-Tirmidhi, and al-Nasa'i narrated, from the hadith of Isma'il ibn Ja'far, from al-'Ala' ibn 'Abd al-Rahman, from his father, from Abu Hurayrah, may Allah be pleased with him, who said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: "Whoever sends a single blessing upon me, Allah will bless him tenfold for it."

Al-Tirmidhi said: This is a hasan sahih (good and authentic) hadith, and on this subject there are reports from 'Abd al-Rahman ibn 'Awf, 'Amir ibn Rabi'ah, 'Ammar, Abu Talhah, Anas, and Ubayy ibn Ka'b.

Imam Ahmad said: Husayn ibn Muhammad narrated to us, Sharik narrated to us, from Layth, from Ka'b, from Abu Hurayrah, from the Prophet ﷺ, who said: "Send blessings upon me, for it is a purification (zakah) for you. And ask Allah to grant me al-Wasilah (the intermediate station), for it is a rank in the highest part of Paradise which none can attain except one man, and I hope that I am that man." Ahmad alone transmitted this. Al-Bazzar narrated it through the route of Mujahid, from Abu Hurayrah, similarly, saying: Muhammad ibn Ishaq al-Bakkali narrated to us, 'Uthman ibn Sa'id narrated to us, Dawud ibn 'Ulayyah narrated to us, from Layth, from Mujahid, from Abu Hurayrah, who said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: "Send blessings upon me, for it is a purification for you, and ask Allah for me the rank, al-Wasilah, from Paradise." So we asked him, or he informed us, and he said: "It is a rank in the highest part of Paradise, and it belongs to one man, and I hope that I am that man."

In its chain is someone who has been criticized.

Another hadith: Imam Ahmad said: Yahya ibn Ishaq narrated to us, Ibn Lahi'ah narrated to us, [from 'Abdullah ibn Hubayrah], from 'Abd al-Rahman ibn Murayj al-Khawlani: I heard Abu Qays, the freedman of 'Amr ibn al-'As, say: I heard 'Abdullah ibn 'Amr say: Whoever sends a single prayer of blessing upon the Messenger of Allah ﷺ, Allah and His angels will bless him seventy times for it, so let a servant do little of that or much. And I heard 'Abdullah ibn 'Amr say: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ came out to us one day as one bidding farewell, and said: "I am Muhammad, the unlettered Prophet," he said this three times, "and there is no prophet after me. I have been given the openings of speech, its conclusions, and its comprehensive statements. I know how many are the keepers of the Fire and the bearers of the Throne. I have been forgiven, and I and my community have been spared. So listen and obey as long as I remain among you. When I am taken from you, hold fast to the Book of Allah: make lawful what it makes lawful and forbid what it forbids."

Another hadith: Abu Dawud al-Tayalisi said: Abu Salamah al-Khurasani narrated to us, Abu Ishaq narrated to us, from Anas, who said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: "Whoever I am mentioned in his presence, let him send blessings upon me. And whoever sends a single blessing upon me, Allah will bless him tenfold."

Al-Nasa'i narrated it in "al-Yawm wa'l-Laylah," from the hadith of Abu Dawud al-Tayalisi, from Abu Salamah, who is al-Mughirah ibn Muslim al-Khurasani, from Abu Ishaq 'Amr ibn 'Abdullah al-Sabi'i, from Anas, with it.

Imam Ahmad said: Muhammad ibn Fudayl narrated to us, Yunus ibn 'Amr, that is, Yunus ibn Abi Ishaq, narrated to us, from Burayd ibn Abi Maryam, from Anas, who said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: "Whoever sends a single blessing upon me, Allah will send ten blessings upon him, and remove from him ten sins."

Another hadith: Imam Ahmad said: 'Abd al-Malik ibn 'Amr and Abu Sa'id narrated to us, [saying]: Sulayman ibn Bilal narrated to us, from 'Umarah ibn Ghaziyyah, from 'Abdullah ibn al-Husayn, from his father 'Ali ibn al-Husayn, from his father, that the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: "The miser is the one in whose presence I am mentioned, and then he does not send blessings upon me." Abu Sa'id said: "then he does not send blessings upon me."

Al-Tirmidhi narrated it from the hadith of Sulayman ibn Bilal, then said: This is a hasan gharib sahih (good, singular, and authentic) hadith.

Some narrators attributed it to the musnad (transmitted collection) of "al-Husayn ibn 'Ali," while others attributed it to the musnad of "'Ali" himself.

Another hadith: Isma'il al-Qadi said: Hajjaj ibn Minhal narrated to us, Hammad ibn Salamah narrated to us, from Ma'bad ibn Hilal al-'Anazi: a man from the people of Damascus narrated to us, from 'Awf ibn Malik, from Abu Dharr, may Allah be pleased with him, that the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: "The most miserly of people is the one in whose presence I am mentioned, and then he does not send blessings upon me."

Another hadith, mursal (with a missing link at the Companion level): Isma'il said: Sulayman ibn Harb narrated to us, Jarir ibn Hazim narrated to us: I heard al-Hasan say: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: "It is enough of miserliness for a man that I be mentioned in his presence and he does not send blessings upon me," may the blessings of Allah be upon him.

Another hadith: Al-Tirmidhi said: Ahmad ibn Ibrahim al-Dawraqi narrated to us, Rib'i ibn Ibrahim narrated to us, from 'Abd al-Rahman ibn Ishaq, from Sa'id ibn Abi Sa'id al-Maqburi, from Abu Hurayrah, who said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: "May the nose of a man be rubbed in the dust, a man in whose presence I was mentioned and he did not send blessings upon me. [And may the nose of a man be rubbed in the dust, a man upon whom the month of Ramadan came and then passed away before he was forgiven]. And may the nose of a man be rubbed in the dust, a man whose two parents reached old age in his presence and he did not thereby enter Paradise." Then he said: hasan gharib.

I say: al-Bukhari narrated it in al-Adab, from Muhammad ibn 'Ubaydullah, Ibn Abi Hazim narrated to us, from Kathir ibn Zayd, from al-Walid ibn Rabah, from Abu Hurayrah, as a raised report (marfu'), similarly. We have also transmitted it from the hadith of Muhammad ibn 'Amr, from Abu Salamah, from Abu Hurayrah, with it. Al-Tirmidhi said: On this subject there are reports from Jabir and Anas.

I say: and from Ibn 'Abbas and Ka'b ibn Ujrah. I have mentioned the routes of this hadith at the beginning of the Book of Fasting and at the verse {Should one of them or both reach old age with you} [al-Isra: 23].

This hadith and the one before it are evidence for the obligation of sending blessings upon him ﷺ whenever he is mentioned, and this is the position of a group of scholars [among them al-Tahawi and al-Halimi]. It is strengthened by the other hadith narrated by Ibn Majah:

Jubarah ibn al-Mughallis narrated to us, Hammad ibn Zayd narrated to us, 'Amr ibn Dinar narrated to us, from Jabir ibn Zayd, from Ibn 'Abbas, who said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: "Whoever forgets to send blessings upon me has erred from the path of Paradise."

Jubarah is weak. But Isma'il al-Qadi narrated it through more than one route, from Abu Ja'far Muhammad ibn 'Ali al-Baqir, who said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: "Whoever forgets to send blessings upon me has erred from the path of Paradise." This is a mursal report strengthened by the one before it [and Allah knows best].

Others held that sending blessings is obligatory once in a gathering, and thereafter is not obligatory for the remainder of that gathering, but rather recommended. Al-Tirmidhi transmitted this from some of them, and it is supported by the hadith narrated by al-Tirmidhi:

Muhammad ibn Bashshar narrated to us, 'Abd al-Rahman narrated to us, Sufyan narrated to us, from Salih, the freedman of al-Taw'amah, from Abu Hurayrah, from the Prophet ﷺ, who said: "No people sit in a gathering in which they do not mention Allah and do not send blessings upon their Prophet, except that it becomes a source of loss for them. If He wills, He punishes them, and if He wills, He forgives them."

Al-Tirmidhi alone transmitted it through this route. Imam Ahmad narrated it from Hajjaj and Yazid ibn Harun, both from Ibn Abi Dhi'b, from Salih, the freedman of al-Taw'amah, from Abu Hurayrah, as a raised report, similarly. Then al-Tirmidhi said: This is a hasan hadith.

It has been narrated from Abu Hurayrah, from the Prophet ﷺ, through more than one route. Isma'il al-Qadi narrated it from the hadith of Shu'bah, from Sulayman, from Dhakwan, from Abu Sa'id, who said: "There is no people who sit and then rise without sending blessings upon the Prophet ﷺ, except that it becomes a source of regret for them, even if they enter Paradise, because of the reward they will see they missed."

It is related from some of them that sending blessings upon him, peace be upon him, is obligatory only once in a lifetime, in compliance with the command of the verse, and thereafter it is recommended in every circumstance. This is the position that al-Qadi 'Iyad supported, after relating the consensus on the obligation of sending blessings upon him ﷺ in general terms. He said: al-Tabarani related that the verse is to be understood as a recommendation, and he claimed consensus on this point.

He said: perhaps that applies to what is beyond the single occurrence, for what is obligatory of it is a single occurrence, like bearing witness to his prophethood, and whatever is beyond that is recommended and encouraged as one of the sunnas of Islam and the distinguishing mark of its people.

I say: this is a strange (gharib) opinion, for the command to send blessings upon him has come at many times, some of them obligatory and some of them recommended, as we shall explain.

Among these is: after the call to prayer, on account of the hadith which the Imam Ahmad narrated:

[chain] Abd Allah ibn Amr ibn al-As said: he heard the Messenger of Allah ﷺ say: "When you hear a caller to prayer, say the like of what he says, then send blessings upon me, for whoever sends one blessing upon me, Allah sends ten blessings upon him for it. Then ask for me the wasilah (intercessory station), for it is a rank in Paradise fit for none but one servant among the servants of Allah, and I hope that I am he. Whoever asks for me the wasilah, intercession becomes due for him."

Muslim, Abu Dawud, al-Tirmidhi, and al-Nasa'i all recorded it from the hadith of Ka'b ibn Alqamah.

Another chain: Isma'il al-Qadi said: [chain] Abd Allah ibn Amr said: the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: "Whoever asks Allah for me the wasilah, my intercession becomes rightfully due for him on the Day of Resurrection."

Another hadith: Isma'il al-Qadi said: [chain] Ka'b, that is Ka'b al-Ahbar, from Abu Hurayrah, may Allah be pleased with him, who said: the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: "Send blessings upon me, for your sending blessings upon me is a purification for you, and ask Allah for me the wasilah." He said: either he narrated to us or we asked him, and he said: "The wasilah is the highest rank in Paradise, attained by none but one man, and I hope that I am that man."

Then he narrated it from Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr, from Mu'tamir, from Layth, that is Ibn Abi Sulaym, with the same chain. And likewise the other hadith:

The Imam Ahmad said: [chain] Ruwayfi' ibn Thabit al-Ansari, that the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: "Whoever sends blessings upon Muhammad and says: O Allah, cause him to descend into the station brought near to You on the Day of Resurrection, my intercession becomes obligatory for him."

This is a chain with no harm in it, though they did not record it.

Another report: Isma'il al-Qadi said: [chain] Ibn Tawus, from his father, who said: I heard Ibn Abbas say: O Allah, accept the greatest intercession of Muhammad, and raise his rank to the highest, and grant him his petition in the Hereafter and in this world, just as You granted Ibrahim and Musa, peace be upon them both. A good, strong, sound chain.

Among this also is: upon entering the mosque and leaving it, on account of the hadith which the Imam Ahmad narrated:

[chain] Fatimah, daughter of the Messenger of Allah ﷺ, said: When the Messenger of Allah ﷺ entered the mosque, he sent blessings and peace upon Muhammad and said: "O Allah, forgive me my sins, and open for me the doors of Your mercy." And when he left, he sent blessings and peace upon Muhammad, then said: "O Allah, forgive me my sins, and open for me the doors of Your bounty."

Isma'il al-Qadi said: [chain] Ali ibn al-Husayn said: Ali ibn Abi Talib, may Allah be pleased with him, said: When you pass by mosques, send blessings upon the Prophet ﷺ.

As for sending blessings upon him ﷺ within the prayer, we have already discussed that in the section on the final tashahhud (testimony), and mentioned the scholars who held that view, along with al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him. As for the first tashahhud, it is not obligatory in it by unanimous agreement, and whether it is recommended there are two opinions from al-Shafi'i.

Among this also is sending blessings upon him ﷺ in the funeral prayer: for the sunna is that one recites the Opening Chapter of the Book at the first takbir (declaration of "Allah is greater"), and at the second one sends blessings upon the Prophet ﷺ, and at the third one supplicates for the deceased, and at the fourth one says: O Allah, do not deprive us of his reward, and do not put us to trial after him.

Al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, said: [chain] a man among the Companions of the Prophet ﷺ informed him that the sunna in the funeral prayer is that the imam says the takbir, then recites the Opening Chapter of the Book silently to himself after the first takbir, then sends blessings upon the Prophet ﷺ, and devotes the supplication sincerely to the deceased, and in the remaining takbirs he recites nothing, then gives the closing salutation silently to himself.

Al-Nasa'i narrated it from Abu Umamah himself, that he said: it is part of the sunna, and he mentioned it.

This, coming from a Companion, has the ruling of a marfu' (elevated) report according to the sound position.

Isma'il al-Qadi narrated it as well, through his chain, from Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab, who said: the sunna in the funeral prayer is... and he mentioned it.

And it has likewise been narrated from Abu Hurayrah, Ibn Umar, and al-Sha'bi.

Among this also is: in the Eid prayer. Isma'il al-Qadi said: [chain] al-Walid ibn Uqbah came out to them one day before the Eid and said to them: this Eid has drawn near, so how is the takbir performed in it? Abd Allah said: you begin by saying a takbir with which you open the prayer, and you praise your Lord and send blessings upon the Prophet ﷺ, then you supplicate, and you say another takbir and do the like of that, then you say another takbir and do the like of that, then you say another takbir and do the like of that, then you recite, then you say a takbir and bow, then you stand and recite, and you praise your Lord and send blessings upon the Prophet ﷺ, then you supplicate and say a takbir and do the like of that, then you bow. Then Hudhayfah and Abu Musa said: Abu Abd al-Rahman has spoken truly. A sound chain.

Among this also is that it is recommended to close supplication with sending blessings upon him ﷺ. Al-Tirmidhi said:

[chain] Umar ibn al-Khattab said: supplication remains suspended between heaven and earth, it does not ascend until you send blessings upon your Prophet.

It was likewise narrated by Ayyub ibn Musa, from Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab, from Umar ibn al-Khattab, as his own statement. And it was narrated by Mu'adh ibn al-Harith, from Abu Qurrah, from Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab, from Umar, as marfu' (elevated to the Prophet). Likewise Razin ibn Mu'awiyah narrated it in his book as marfu', from the Prophet ﷺ, who said: "Supplication remains suspended between heaven and earth, it does not ascend until blessings are sent upon me. So do not treat me like the water-skin of the rider; send blessings upon me at the beginning of the supplication, its middle, and its end."

This addition is narrated only through the report of Jabir ibn Abd Allah in the Musnad of the Imam Abd ibn Humayd al-Kashshi, where he said: [chain] Jabir said: the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said to us: "Do not treat me like the drinking-vessel of the rider: when he hangs up his gear, he takes his vessel and fills it with water, and if he has need of it for ablution he performs ablution, and if he has need of it for drinking he drinks, and otherwise he pours out what is in it. Place me at the beginning of the supplication, in the middle of the supplication, and at the end of the supplication." This is a gharib (singular) hadith, and Musa ibn Ubaydah is weak in hadith.

Among the most emphasized of this is the supplication of qunut, on account of what the Imam Ahmad, the authors of the Sunan works, Ibn Khuzaymah, Ibn Hibban, and al-Hakim narrated from the hadith of Abu al-Hawra, from al-Hasan ibn Ali, may Allah be pleased with them both, who said: the Messenger of Allah ﷺ taught me words to say in the witr prayer: "O Allah, guide me among those You have guided, grant me well-being among those You have granted well-being, take charge of me among those You have taken charge of, bless for me what You have given, protect me from the evil of what You have decreed, for indeed You decree and none decrees over You, and none whom You have taken as an ally is humiliated. Blessed are You, our Lord, and exalted."

Al-Nasa'i added in his Sunan after this: and may Allah send blessings upon the Prophet Muhammad.

Among that is: it is recommended to increase the sending of salawat upon him on Friday and on the night preceding Friday.

Imam Ahmad said: Husayn ibn Ali al-Jufi narrated to us, from Abd al-Rahman ibn Yazid ibn Jabir, from Abu al-Ash'ath al-San'ani, from Aws ibn Aws al-Thaqafi, may Allah be pleased with him, who said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: "Among the best of your days is Friday. On it Adam was created, and on it he died, and on it is the Blowing of the Trumpet, and on it is the Swoon (al-sa'qah). So send abundant salawat upon me on it, for your salawat are presented to me." They said: O Messenger of Allah, how will our salawat be presented to you when you have decayed, meaning: when your body has worn away? He said: "Indeed Allah has forbidden the earth to consume the bodies of the prophets."

Abu Dawud, al-Nasa'i, and Ibn Majah narrated it from the hadith of Husayn ibn Ali al-Jufi. Ibn Khuzaymah, Ibn Hibban, al-Daraqutni, and al-Nawawi in al-Adhkar have graded this hadith sound.

Another hadith: Abu Abdullah Ibn Majah said: Amr ibn Sawwad al-Misri narrated to us, Abdullah ibn Wahb narrated to us, from Amr ibn al-Harith, from Sa'id ibn Abi Hilal, from Zayd ibn Ayman, from Ubadah ibn Nusayy, from Abu al-Darda, who said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: "Send abundant salawat upon me on Friday, for it is a witnessed day, the angels witness it, and no one sends salawat upon me except that his salawat is presented to me until he finishes it." He said: I said: Even after death? He said: "[Even after death], for Allah has forbidden the earth to consume the bodies of the prophets, [so the prophet of Allah is alive, provided with sustenance]."

This is a gharib (singular) hadith from this route, and it contains a disconnection (inqita') between Ubadah ibn Nusayy and Abu al-Darda, for he did not meet him. And Allah knows best.

Al-Bayhaqi narrated from the hadith of Abu Umamah and Abu Mas'ud, from the Prophet ﷺ, concerning the command to increase salawat upon him on the night of Friday and on Friday, but in both their chains there is weakness. And Allah knows best.

It has also been reported as mursal (a report with the Companion link omitted) from al-Hasan al-Basri. Isma'il al-Qadi said: Sulayman ibn Harb narrated to us, Jarir ibn Hazim narrated to us, I heard al-Hasan, that is al-Basri, saying: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: "The earth does not consume the body of one whom the Holy Spirit (Ruh al-Qudus) has spoken to." This is a hasan mursal report.

Al-Shafi'i said: Ibrahim ibn Muhammad informed us, Safwan ibn Sulaym informed us, that the Prophet ﷺ said: "When it is Friday and the night of Friday, send abundant salawat upon me." This is mursal.

And thus it is obligatory upon the khatib (one delivering the sermon) to send salawat upon the Prophet ﷺ on Friday on the pulpit during both sermons, and the two sermons are not valid except with that, because it is an act of worship, and the mention of Allah in it is a condition, so the mention of the Messenger ﷺ in it becomes obligatory, just as in the call to prayer and in the prayer itself. This is the school of al-Shafi'i and Ahmad, may Allah have mercy on both of them.

Among that also is: it is recommended to send salawat and salam upon him at the visiting of his grave, the salawat and salam of Allah be upon him.

Abu Dawud said: Ibn Awf, that is Muhammad, narrated to us, al-Muqri narrated to us, Haywah narrated to us, from Abu Sakhr Humayd ibn Ziyad, from Yazid ibn Abdullah ibn Qusayt, from Abu Hurayrah, that the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: "There is no one who greets me with salam except that Allah returns my soul to me, so that I may return the greeting to him."

Abu Dawud narrated this alone (tafarrada), and al-Nawawi graded it sound in al-Adhkar. Then Abu Dawud said: Ahmad ibn Salih narrated to us, saying: I read to Abdullah ibn Nafi', Ibn Abi Dhi'b informed me, from Sa'id al-Maqburi, from Abu Hurayrah, who said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: "Do not turn your houses into graves, and do not turn my grave into a festival (id), and send salawat upon me, for your salawat reach me wherever you are."

Abu Dawud narrated this alone as well. Imam Ahmad narrated it from Surayj, from Abdullah ibn Nafi' (who is al-Sa'igh), with the same chain. Al-Nawawi also graded it sound.

It has also been narrated by another route from Ali, may Allah be pleased with him. The judge Isma'il ibn Ishaq said in his book "The Merit of Sending Salawat upon the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace":

Isma'il ibn Abi Uways narrated to us, Ja'far ibn Ibrahim ibn Muhammad ibn Ali ibn Abdullah ibn Ja'far ibn Abi Talib narrated to us, from someone who informed him among the people of his household, from Ali ibn al-Husayn ibn Ali: that a man used to come every morning and visit the grave of the Prophet ﷺ and send salawat upon him, and would do things in that regard which became well known, so that Ali ibn al-Husayn heard about him. Ali ibn al-Husayn said to him: What drives you to do this? He said: I love to send greeting of peace upon the Prophet ﷺ. Ali ibn al-Husayn said to him: Would you like me to relate to you a hadith from my father? He said: Yes. Ali ibn al-Husayn said to him: My father informed me, from my grandfather, that he said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: "Do not turn my grave into a festival, and do not turn your houses into graves, and send salawat and salam upon me wherever you are, for your salawat and salam reach me."

In its chain there is an unidentified man who is not named. It has also been narrated by another route as mursal. Abd al-Razzaq said in his Musannaf, from al-Thawri, from Ibn Ajlan, from a man called Suhayl, from al-Hasan ibn al-Hasan ibn Ali: that he saw a group of people at the grave and forbade them, saying: The Prophet ﷺ said: "Do not take my grave as a festival, and do not take your houses as graves, and send salawat upon me wherever you are, for your salawat reach me." Perhaps he saw them behaving with poor manners by raising their voices beyond what was needed, so he forbade them.

It has also been reported that he saw a man frequently visiting the grave, and said: O you, you and a man in al-Andalus are exactly the same in this regard, meaning: it reaches him equally from all, may the salawat and salam of Allah be upon him always until the Day of Judgment.

Al-Tabarani said in his al-Mu'jam al-Kabir: Ahmad ibn Rishdin al-Misri narrated to us, Sa'id ibn Abi Maryam narrated to us, Muhammad ibn Ja'far narrated to us, Humayd ibn Abi Zaynab informed me, from Hasan ibn Hasan ibn Ali ibn Abi Talib, may Allah be pleased with them, from his father: that the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: "Send salawat upon me wherever you are, for your salawat reach me."

Al-Tabarani then said: al-Abbas ibn Himdan al-Asbahani narrated to us, Shu'ayb ibn Abd al-Hamid al-Tahhan narrated to us, Yazid ibn Harun informed us, from Shayban, from al-Hakam ibn Abdullah ibn Khattaf, from Umm Unays bint al-Hasan ibn Ali, from her father, who said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: "Have you considered the saying of Allah, mighty and majestic: {Indeed Allah and His angels send salawat upon the Prophet}?" He said: "This is the concealed matter, and had you not asked me about it I would not have informed you of it. Indeed Allah has assigned to me two angels, I am not mentioned in the presence of a Muslim servant who sends salawat upon me, except that those two angels say: 'May Allah forgive you.' And Allah and His angels say, in answer to those two angels: 'Amin.' And no one sends salawat except that those two angels say: 'May Allah forgive you,' and Allah and His angels say, in answer to those two angels: 'Amin.'"

This is exceedingly gharib, and its chain contains severe weakness.

Imam Ahmad said: Waki' narrated to us, from Sufyan, from Abdullah ibn al-Sa'ib, from Zadhan, from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, may Allah be pleased with him: that the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: "Indeed Allah has angels who travel about the earth, conveying to me the greetings of salam from my ummah."

Al-Nasa'i likewise narrated it from the hadith of Sufyan al-Thawri and Sulayman ibn Mihran al-A'mash, both of them from Abdullah ibn al-Sa'ib, with the same chain.

As for the other hadith: "Whoever sends salawat upon me at my grave, I hear it, and whoever sends salawat upon me from afar, it is conveyed to me," there is doubt in its chain. Muhammad ibn Marwan al-Suddi al-Saghir narrated it alone, and he is discarded (matruk) as a narrator, from al-A'mash, from Abu Salih, from Abu Hurayrah, as a marfu' (elevated) report.

Our companions (scholars of the school) said: it is recommended for the muhrim (one in the state of ihram), when he recites the talbiyah and finishes it, to send salawat upon the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, based on what was reported from al-Shafi'i and al-Daraqutni, from the narration of Salih ibn Muhammad ibn Za'idah, from al-Qasim ibn Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr al-Siddiq, who said: A man was commanded, when he finished his talbiyah, to send salawat upon the Prophet ﷺ in every circumstance.

Isma'il al-Qadi said: Arim ibn al-Fadl narrated to us, Abdullah ibn al-Mubarak narrated to us, Zakariyya narrated to us, from al-Sha'bi, from Wahb ibn al-Ajda', who said: I heard Umar ibn al-Khattab say: When you arrive, circle the House seven times, and pray two rak'ahs at the Maqam, then go to al-Safa and stand upon it from where you can see the House, and say "Allahu akbar" seven times, a takbir between praising Allah and extolling Him, sending salawat upon the Prophet ﷺ, and asking a request for yourself, and do the same at al-Marwah.

This is a good, sound, and strong chain of transmission.

They said: it is also recommended to send salawat upon the Prophet ﷺ along with the mention of Allah at the time of slaughtering, and they took support from His saying, Exalted is He: {And We raised for you your remembrance} [al-Sharh: 4]. Some of the commentators said: Allah, Exalted is He, says: "I am not remembered except that you are remembered along with Me." The majority disagreed with them on this and said: this is a station in which the remembrance of the Lord, Exalted is He, is to be singled out alone, just as at eating, entering a place, intercourse, and other such matters, for which no sunnah has come reporting the sending of salawat upon the Prophet ﷺ.

Another hadith: Isma'il al-Qadi said: Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr al-Muqaddimi narrated to us, Umar ibn Harun narrated to us, from Musa ibn Ubaydah, from Muhammad ibn Thabit, from Abu Hurayrah, that the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: "Send salawat upon the prophets of Allah and His messengers, for Allah sent them just as He sent me."

In its chain there are two weak narrators, namely Umar ibn Harun and his teacher, and Allah knows best. It has also been narrated by Abd al-Razzaq, from al-Thawri, from Musa ibn Ubaydah al-Rabadhi, with the same content.

Among such matters: it is recommended to send salawat upon him when the ear rings, if the report concerning that is authentic, given that the imam Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn Ishaq ibn Khuzaymah narrated it in his Sahih, saying: Ziyad ibn Yahya narrated to us, Ma'mar ibn Muhammad ibn Ubaydullah narrated to us, from his father Muhammad, from his father Abu Rafi', who said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: "When the ear of one of you rings, let him remember me and send salawat upon me, and let him say: 'May Allah remember with good whoever remembers me with good.'" Its chain of transmission is gharib (singular), and there is doubt about its establishment. Allah knows best.

[Here is a matter to note]:

The people of writing have recommended that the scribe repeat the salawat upon the Prophet, may Allah's peace and blessings be upon him, every time he writes it. It has come in a hadith by way of Kadih ibn Rahmah, from Nahshal, from al-Dahhak, from Ibn Abbas, who said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: "Whoever sends salawat upon me in a book, the salawat will continue flowing for him as long as my name remains in that book."

This hadith is not sound for many reasons. It has also been narrated from the hadith of Abu Hurayrah, and that too is not sound. The hafiz Abu Abdullah al-Dhahabi, our teacher, said: I consider it fabricated. Something similar has also been narrated from Abu Bakr and from Ibn Abbas, and none of that is sound. Allah knows best. Al-Khatib al-Baghdadi mentioned in his book al-Jami' li-Adab al-Rawi wa'l-Sami': I saw in the handwriting of the imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal, may Allah have mercy on him, that he often wrote the name of the Prophet ﷺ without mentioning the salawat upon him in writing. He said: and it has reached me that he used to say the salawat aloud instead.

[Section]

As for sending salawat upon someone other than the prophets, if it is done in a manner of being subordinate, as came earlier in the hadith: "O Allah, send salawat upon Muhammad and his family, his wives, and his descendants," then this is permissible by consensus. The dispute arose only concerning singling out someone other than the prophets for salawat on their own. Some said: this is permissible, and they argued with His saying: {He it is who sends salawat upon you, and His angels} and with His saying: {upon them are salawat from their Lord, and mercy} [al-Baqarah: 157], and with His saying, Exalted is He: {Take from their wealth a charity by which you purify them and cleanse them, and pray for them (send salawat upon them); indeed your prayer is a source of tranquility for them} [al-Tawbah: 103], and with the hadith of Abdullah ibn Abi Awfa, who said: When the Messenger of Allah ﷺ was brought people's charity, he would say: "O Allah, send salawat upon them." My father came to him with his charity, and he said: "O Allah, send salawat upon the family of Abu Awfa." Both of them narrated it in the two Sahihs. And with the hadith of Jabir, that his wife said: O Messenger of Allah, send salawat upon me and upon my husband. He said: "May Allah send salawat upon you and upon your husband."

The majority of the scholars said: it is not permissible to single out anyone other than the prophets for salawat, because this has become a distinguishing symbol for the prophets when they are mentioned, and others are not to be joined with them in this. So one does not say: "Abu Bakr said, may Allah's salawat be upon him," or "Ali said, may Allah's salawat be upon him," even though the meaning would be correct, just as one does not say "Muhammad, Mighty and Majestic is He," even though he is indeed mighty and majestic, because that phrase is a distinguishing symbol for the remembrance of Allah, Mighty and Majestic. They interpreted what has come in the Book and the Sunnah concerning this as being a supplication for them, and this is why it was not established as a distinguishing symbol for the family of Abu Awfa, nor for Jabir and his wife. This is a sound approach.

Others said: this is not permissible, because sending salawat upon someone other than the prophets has become a distinguishing symbol of the people of deviant sects, who send salawat upon those in whom they hold certain beliefs, and they are not to be followed in that. Allah knows best.

Then those who prohibited this differed as to whether it falls under the category of prohibition, disliked but not forbidden (karahah tanzihiyyah), or contrary to what is preferable. There are three opinions on this, as related by the shaykh Abu Zakariyya al-Nawawi in the book al-Adhkar. He then said: the correct view, held by the majority, is that it is disliked in the sense of karahah tanzihiyyah, because it has become a distinguishing symbol of the people of innovation, and we have been forbidden from adopting their symbols. What is disliked is that for which an intended prohibition has come. Our companions said: the relied-upon reasoning in this matter is that salawat has become specifically associated in speech with the prophets, may Allah's blessings and peace be upon them, just as our saying "Mighty and Majestic is He" is specifically associated with Allah, Glorified and Exalted is He. Just as one does not say "Muhammad, Mighty and Majestic is He," even though he is indeed mighty and majestic, one does not say "Abu Bakr" or "Ali, may Allah's salawat be upon him." This is his wording exactly, letter for letter. He said: as for the greeting of salam, the shaykh Abu Muhammad al-Juwayni, one of our companions, said: it carries the same meaning as salawat, so it is not used for someone absent, and it is not singled out for anyone other than the prophets. So one does not say "Ali, peace be upon him," and this applies equally to the living and the dead. As for someone present, they are addressed with it directly, so one says: "peace be upon you" (plural) or "peace be upon you" (singular), or "the peace be upon you" in either form. This is a matter of consensus. This concludes what he mentioned.

I say: this practice has become widespread in the expressions used by many copyists of books, singling out Ali, may Allah be pleased with him, by saying "peace be upon him," apart from the rest of the companions, or saying "may Allah honor his face," and although the meaning of this is correct, all the companions should be treated equally in this regard, for this falls under the category of honoring and venerating, and the two shaykhs (Abu Bakr and Umar) and the Commander of the Faithful Uthman ibn Affan are more deserving of this than he is, may Allah be pleased with all of them.

Isma'il al-Qadi said: Abdullah ibn Abd al-Wahhab narrated to us, Abd al-Wahid ibn Ziyad narrated to us, Uthman ibn Hakim ibn Abbad ibn Hunayf narrated to me, from Ikrimah, from Ibn Abbas, that he said: it is not correct to send salawat upon anyone except the Prophet ﷺ, but rather one prays for forgiveness for the Muslim men and Muslim women.

He also said: Abu Bakr ibn Abi Shaybah narrated to us, Husayn ibn Ali narrated to us, from Ja'far ibn Burqan, who said: Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz, may Allah have mercy on him, wrote: To proceed, some people have sought the world through deeds of the hereafter, and some of the storytellers have introduced an innovation of sending salawat upon their caliphs and rulers equal to the salawat upon the Prophet ﷺ. When this letter of mine reaches you, order them that their salawat be upon the prophets, and their supplication be for the Muslims in general, and let them abandon anything besides that. A good report.

Isma'il al-Qadi said: Mu'adh ibn Asad narrated to us, Abdullah ibn al-Mubarak narrated to us, Ibn Lahi'ah narrated to us, Khalid ibn Yazid narrated to me, from Sa'id ibn Abi Hilal, from Nubayh ibn Wahb, that Ka'b entered upon Aishah, may Allah be pleased with her, and they mentioned the Messenger of Allah ﷺ, and Ka'b said: there is no dawn that breaks except that seventy thousand angels descend and surround the grave, beating their wings and sending salawat upon the Prophet ﷺ, seventy thousand by night and seventy thousand by day, until when the earth splits open for him, he will come forth amid seventy thousand angels escorting him joyfully.

[Branch]

Al-Nawawi said: When one invokes blessings upon the Prophet ﷺ, he should combine the salah (blessing) with the taslim (salutation of peace), and should not restrict himself to only one of the two. So he should not say "sallallahu 'alayhi" (may Allah bless him) alone, nor "'alayhi al-salam" (peace be upon him) alone. What he has said here is drawn from this noble verse, namely His saying: {O you who believe, invoke blessings upon him and salute him with a worthy salutation}. So it is more fitting to say: ﷺ, with a proper salutation of peace.

### Source (Arabic) — review against this

قَالَ الْبُخَارِيُّ: قَالَ أَبُو الْعَالِيَةِ: صَلَاةُ اللَّهِ: ثَنَاؤُهُ عَلَيْهِ عِنْدَ الْمَلَائِكَةِ، وَصَلَاةُ الْمَلَائِكَةِ: الدُّعَاءُ. وَقَالَ ابْنُ عَبَّاسٍ: يُصَلُّونَ: يبرِّكون. هَكَذَا عَلَّقَهُ الْبُخَارِيُّ عَنْهُمَا .

وَقَدْ رَوَاهُ أَبُو جَعْفَرٍ الرَّازِيُّ، عَنِ الرَّبِيعِ بْنِ أَنَسٍ، عَنْ أَبِي الْعَالِيَةِ كَذَلِكَ. وَرُوِيَ مِثْلُهُ عَنِ الرَّبِيعِ أَيْضًا. وَرَوَى عَلِيُّ بْنُ أَبِي طَلْحَةَ، عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ كَمَا قَالَهُ سَوَاءً، رَوَاهُمَا ابْنُ أَبِي حَاتِمٍ.

وَقَالَ أَبُو عِيسَى التِّرْمِذِيُّ: وَرُوِيَ عَنْ سُفْيَانَ الثَّوْرِيِّ وَغَيْرِ وَاحِدٍ مِنْ أَهْلِ الْعِلْمِ قَالُوا: صَلَاةُ الرَّبِّ: الرَّحْمَةُ، وَصَلَاةُ الْمَلَائِكَةِ: الِاسْتِغْفَارُ.

ثُمَّ قَالَ ابْنُ أَبِي حَاتِمٍ: حَدَّثَنَا عَمْرٌو الأوْديّ، حَدَّثَنَا وَكِيع، عَنِ الْأَعْمَشِ، عَنْ عَمْرِو بْنِ مُرَّةَ، قَالَ الْأَعْمَشُ عَنْ عَطَاءِ بْنِ أَبِي رَبَاحٍ ﴿إِنَّ اللَّهَ وَمَلائِكَتَهُ يُصَلُّونَ عَلَى النَّبِيِّ﴾ قَالَ: صَلَاتُهُ تَبَارَكَ وَتَعَالَى: سُبّوح قُدُّوسٌ، سَبَقَتْ رَحْمَتِي غَضَبِي.

وَالْمَقْصُودُ مِنْ هَذِهِ الْآيَةِ: أَنَّ اللَّهَ سُبْحَانَهُ أَخْبَرَ عِبَادَهُ بِمَنْزِلَةِ عَبْدِهِ وَنَبِيِّهِ عِنْدَهُ فِي الْمَلَأِ الْأَعْلَى، بِأَنَّهُ يُثْنِي عَلَيْهِ عِنْدَ الْمَلَائِكَةِ الْمُقَرَّبِينَ، وَأَنَّ الْمَلَائِكَةَ تُصَلِّي عَلَيْهِ. ثُمَّ أَمَرَ تَعَالَى أَهْلَ الْعَالَمِ السُّفْلِيِّ بِالصَّلَاةِ وَالتَّسْلِيمِ عَلَيْهِ، لِيَجْتَمِعَ الثَّنَاءَ عَلَيْهِ مِنْ أَهْلِ الْعَالَمِينَ الْعُلْوِيِّ وَالسُّفْلِيِّ جَمِيعًا.

وَقَدْ قَالَ ابْنُ أَبِي حَاتِمٍ: حَدَّثَنَا عَلِيُّ بْنُ الْحُسَيْنِ، حَدَّثَنَا أَحْمَدُ بْنُ عَبْدِ الرَّحْمَنِ، حَدَّثَنِي أَبِي، عَنْ أَبِيهِ، عَنْ أَشْعَثَ بْنِ إِسْحَاقَ، عَنْ جَعْفَرٍ - يَعْنِي: ابْنَ الْمُغِيرَةِ -عَنْ سَعِيدِ بْنِ جُبَيْرٍ، عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ: أَنَّ بَنِي إِسْرَائِيلَ قَالُوا لِمُوسَى عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ: هَلْ يُصَلِّي رَبُّكَ؟ فَنَادَاهُ رَبُّهُ: يَا مُوسَى، سَأَلُوكَ: "هَلْ يُصَلِّي رَبُّكَ؟ " فَقُلْ: نَعَمْ، إِنَّمَا أُصَلِّي أَنَا وَمَلَائِكَتِي عَلَى أَنْبِيَائِي وَرُسُلِي. فَأَنْزَلَ اللَّهُ عَزَّ وَجَلَّ، عَلَى نَبِيِّهِ ﷺ: ﴿إِنَّ اللَّهَ وَمَلائِكَتَهُ يُصَلُّونَ عَلَى النَّبِيِّ يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا صَلُّوا عَلَيْهِ وَسَلِّمُوا تَسْلِيمًا﴾ .

وَقَدْ أَخْبَرَ أَنَّهُ سُبْحَانَهُ وَتَعَالَى ، يُصَلِّي عَلَى عِبَادِهِ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ فِي قَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى: ﴿يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا اذْكُرُوا اللَّهَ ذِكْرًا كَثِيرًا وَسَبِّحُوهُ بُكْرَةً وَأَصِيلا. هُوَ الَّذِي يُصَلِّي عَلَيْكُمْ وَمَلائِكَتُهُ لِيُخْرِجَكُمْ مِنَ الظُّلُمَاتِ إِلَى النُّورِ وَكَانَ بِالْمُؤْمِنِينَ رَحِيمًا﴾ [الْأَحْزَابِ:٤١-٤٣] . وَقَالَ تَعَالَى: ﴿وَبَشِّرِ الصَّابِرِينَ . الَّذِينَ إِذَا أَصَابَتْهُمْ مُصِيبَةٌ قَالُوا إِنَّا لِلَّهِ وَإِنَّا إِلَيْهِ رَاجِعُونَ. أُولَئِكَ عَلَيْهِمْ صَلَوَاتٌ مِنْ رَبِّهِمْ وَرَحْمَةٌ وَأُولَئِكَ هُمُ الْمُهْتَدُونَ﴾ [الْبَقَرَةِ: ١٥٥-١٥٧] . وَفِي الْحَدِيثِ: "إِنَّ اللَّهَ وملائكته يصلون على ميامِن الصفوف". وفي الْحَدِيثِ الْآخَرِ: "اللَّهُمَّ، صَلِّ عَلَى آلِ أَبِي أَوْفَى". وَقَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ لِامْرَأَةِ جَابِرٍ -وَقَدْ سَأَلْتُهُ أَنْ يُصَلِّيَ عَلَيْهَا وَعَلَى زَوْجِهَا -"صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْكَ، وَعَلَى زَوْجِكَ .

وَقَدْ جَاءَتِ الْأَحَادِيثُ الْمُتَوَاتِرَةُ عَنْ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ ﷺ بِالْأَمْرِ بِالصَّلَاةِ عَلَيْهِ، وَكَيْفِيَّةِ الصَّلَاةِ عَلَيْهِ، وَنَحْنُ نَذْكُرُ مِنْهَا إِنْ شَاءَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى مَا تَيَسَّرَ، وَاللَّهُ الْمُسْتَعَانُ.

قَالَ الْبُخَارِيُّ -عِنْدَ تَفْسِيرِ هَذِهِ الْآيَةِ -: حَدَّثَنَا سَعِيدُ بْنُ يَحْيَى بْنِ سَعِيدٍ، حَدَّثَنَا أَبِي، عَنْ مِسْعَر، عَنِ الْحَكَمِ، عَنِ ابْنِ أَبِي لَيْلَى، عَنْ كَعْبِ بْنِ عُجْرَة قَالَ: قِيلَ: يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ، أَمَّا السَّلَامُ عَلَيْكَ فَقد عَرَفْنَاهُ، فَكَيْفَ الصَّلَاةُ؟ فَقَالَ: "قُولُوا: اللَّهُمَّ، صِلِّ عَلَى مُحَمَّدٍ، وَعَلَى آلِ مُحَمَّدٍ، [كَمَا صَلَّيْتَ عَلَى آلِ إِبْرَاهِيمَ، إِنَّكَ حَمِيدٌ مَجِيدٌ. اللَّهُمَّ، بَارِكْ عَلَى مُحَمَّدٍ وَعَلَى آلِ مُحَمَّدٍ] كَمَا بَارَكْتَ عَلَى آلِ إِبْرَاهِيمَ، إِنَّكَ حَمِيدٌ مَجِيدٌ" .

وَقَالَ الْإِمَامُ أَحْمَدُ: حَدَّثَنَا مُحَمَّدُ بْنُ جَعْفَرٍ، حَدَّثَنَا شُعْبَةُ ، عَنِ الْحَكَمِ قَالَ: سَمِعْتُ ابْنَ أَبِي لَيْلَى قَالَ: لَقِيَنِي كَعْبُ بْنُ عُجْرَةَ فَقَالَ: أَلَا أَهْدِي لَكَ هَدِيَّةً؟ خَرَجَ عَلَيْنَا رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ فَقُلْنَا: يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ، قَدْ عَلِمْنَا -أَوْ: عَرَفْنَا -كَيْفَ السَّلَامُ ، عَلَيْكَ، فَكَيْفَ الصَّلَاةُ؟ قَالَ: "قُولُوا: اللَّهُمَّ، صِلِّ عَلَى مُحَمَّدٍ وَعَلَى آلِ مُحَمَّدٍ، كَمَا صَلَّيْتَ عَلَى [آلِ] إِبْرَاهِيمَ إِنَّكَ حَمِيدٌ مَجِيدٌ. اللَّهُمَّ، بَارِكْ عَلَى مُحَمَّدٍ وَعَلَى آلِ مُحَمَّدٍ، كَمَا بَارَكْتَ على آل إبراهيم، إِنَّكَ حَمِيدٌ مَجِيدٌ".

وَهَذَا الْحَدِيثُ قَدْ أَخْرَجَهُ الْجَمَاعَةُ فِي كُتُبِهِمْ، مِنْ طُرُقٍ مُتَعَدِّدَةٍ، عَنِ الْحَكَمِ -وَهُوَ ابْنُ عُتْبَةَ زَادَ الْبُخَارِيُّ: وَعَبْدُ اللَّهِ بْنُ عِيسَى، كِلَاهُمَا عَنْ عَبْدِ الرَّحْمَنِ بْنِ أَبِي لَيْلَى، فَذَكَرَهُ .

وَقَالَ ابْنُ أَبِي حَاتِمٍ : حَدَّثَنَا الْحَسَنُ بْنُ عَرَفَةَ، حَدَّثَنَا هُشَيْم بْنُ بُشَير، عَنْ يَزِيدَ بْنِ أَبِي زِيَادٍ، حَدَّثَنَا عَبْدِ الرَّحْمَنِ بْنِ أَبِي لَيْلَى، عَنْ كَعْبِ بْنِ عُجْرَة قَالَ: لَمَّا نَزَلَتْ: ﴿إِنَّ اللَّهَ وَمَلائِكَتَهُ يُصَلُّونَ عَلَى النَّبِيِّ يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا صَلُّوا عَلَيْهِ وَسَلِّمُوا تَسْلِيمًا﴾ . قَالَ: قُلْنَا: يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ، قَدْ عَلِمْنَا السَّلَامَ فَكَيْفَ الصَّلَاةُ عَلَيْكَ؟ قَالَ: "قُولُوا: اللَّهُمَّ صِلِّ عَلَى مُحَمَّدٍ وَعَلَى آلِ مُحَمَّدٍ، كَمَا صَلَّيْتَ عَلَى إِبْرَاهِيمَ وَعَلَى آلِ إِبْرَاهِيمَ، إِنَّكَ حَمِيدٌ مَجِيدٌ. وَبَارِكْ عَلَى مُحَمَّدٍ وَعَلَى آلِ مُحَمَّدٍ، كَمَا بَارَكْتَ عَلَى إِبْرَاهِيمَ وَعَلَى آلِ إِبْرَاهِيمَ. إِنَّكَ حَمِيدٌ مَجِيدٌ". وَكَانَ عَبْدُ الرَّحْمَنِ بْنُ أَبِي لَيْلَى يَقُولُ: وَعَلَيْنَا مَعَهُمْ.

وَرَوَاهُ التِّرْمِذِيُّ بِهَذِهِ الزِّيَادَةِ .

وَمَعْنَى قَوْلِهِمْ: "أَمَّا السَّلَامُ عَلَيْكَ فَقَدْ عَرَفْنَاهُ": هُوَ الَّذِي فِي التَّشَهُّدِ الَّذِي كَانَ يُعَلِّمُهُمْ إِيَّاهُ، كَمَا كَانَ يُعَلِّمُهُمُ السُّورَةَ مِنَ الْقُرْآنِ، وَفِيهِ: "السَّلَامُ عَلَيْكَ أَيُّهَا النَّبِيُّ وَرَحْمَةُ اللَّهِ وَبَرَكَاتُهُ".

حَدِيثٌ آخَرُ: قَالَ الْبُخَارِيُّ: حَدَّثَنَا عَبْدُ اللَّهِ بْنُ يُوسُفَ، حَدَّثَنَا اللَّيْثُ، عَنِ ابْنُ الْهَادِ، عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ خَبَّابٍ، عَنْ أَبِي سَعِيدٍ الْخُدْرِيِّ، رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ، قَالَ: قُلْنَا: يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ، هَذَا السَّلَامُ فَكَيْفَ نُصَلِّي عَلَيْكَ: قَالَ: "قُولُوا: اللَّهُمَّ صَلِّ عَلَى مُحَمَّدٍ عَبْدِكَ وَرَسُولِكَ، كَمَا صَلَّيْتَ عَلَى آلِ إِبْرَاهِيمَ. وَبَارِكْ عَلَى مُحَمَّدٍ وَعَلَى آلِ مُحَمَّدٍ، كَمَا بَارَكَتْ عَلَى آلِ إِبْرَاهِيمَ". [وَفِي رِوَايَةٍ] : قَالَ أَبُو صَالِحٍ، عَنِ اللَّيْثِ: "عَلَى مُحَمَّدٍ وَعَلَى آلِ مُحَمَّدٍ، كَمَا بَارَكْتَ على آلِ إِبْرَاهِيمَ".

حَدَّثَنَا إِبْرَاهِيمُ بْنُ حَمْزَةَ، حَدَّثَنَا ابْنُ أَبِي حَازِمٍ والدّرَاوَرْدي، عَنْ يَزِيدَ -يَعْنِي: ابْنَ الْهَادِ -قَالَ: "كَمَا صَلَّيْتَ عَلَى إِبْرَاهِيمَ، وَبَارِكْ عَلَى مُحَمَّدٍ وَآلِ مُحَمَّدٍ، كَمَا بَارَكْتَ عَلَى إِبْرَاهِيمَ وَآلِ إِبْرَاهِيمَ".

وَأَخْرَجَهُ النَّسَائِيُّ وَابْنُ مَاجَهْ، مِنْ حَدِيثِ ابْنِ الْهَادِ، بِهِ .

حَدِيثٌ آخَرُ: قَالَ الْإِمَامُ أَحْمَدُ: قَرَأْتُ عَلَى عَبْدِ الرَّحْمَنِ: مَالِكٌ، عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ أَبِي بَكْرٍ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ، عَنْ عَمْرِو بْنِ سُلَيم أَنَّهُ قَالَ: أَخْبَرَنِي أَبُو حُمَيْدٍ السَّاعِدِيُّ أَنَّهُمْ قَالُوا: يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ، كَيْفَ نُصَلِّي عَلَيْكَ؟ قَالَ: "قُولُوا: اللَّهُمَّ" صَلِّ عَلَى مُحَمَّدٍ وَأَزْوَاجِهِ وَذُرِّيَّتِهِ، كَمَا صَلَّيْتَ عَلَى [آلِ] إِبْرَاهِيمَ، وَبَارِكْ عَلَى مُحَمَّدٍ وَأَزْوَاجِهِ وَذُرِّيَّتِهِ، كَمَا بَارَكْتَ عَلَى آلِ إِبْرَاهِيمَ، إِنَّكَ حَمِيدٌ مَجِيدٌ".

وَقَدْ أَخْرَجَهُ بَقِيَّةُ الْجَمَاعَةِ، سِوَى التِّرْمِذِيِّ، مِنْ حَدِيثِ مَالِكٍ، بِهِ .
